    [Original] Trividia Health, Inc. Initiates Labeling Correction for all TRUE METRIXÂ® Blood Glucose Monitoring Systems
    Trividia Health, Inc. announced on February 6, 2026, a labeling correction for its TRUE METRIX, TRUE METRIX AIR, TRUE METRIX GO, and TRUE METRIX PRO Blood Glucose Monitoring Systems distributed in the U.S., U.K., Mexico, Australia, and the Caribbean. The update modifies the E-5 Error Code instructions in Ownerâ€™s Booklets and System Instructions for Use to emphasize that users must seek immediate medical attention if they receive an E-5 error code while experiencing symptoms of high glucose, such as fatigue, excessive urination, thirst, or blurry vision. The E-5 error indicates either a blood glucose level exceeding 600 mg/dL or a test strip error. Previously, the instructions did not sufficiently stress the urgency of medical intervention in symptomatic cases, potentially leading to delayed treatment and serious health risks, including death. Since the productâ€™s global launch in August 2014, 114 serious injuries and one death have been reported linked to the E-5 error. Updated instructions now require users to retest with a new strip; if the error persists and symptoms are present, medical attention is required immediately. If no symptoms exist, retesting is advised, and persistent errors should prompt a call to Trividiaâ€™s customer support at 1-800-803-6025 (Monâ€“Fri, 8 AMâ€“8 PM EST). The correction applies to all branded and co-branded products sold under retail partnersâ€™ names. Trividia is distributing a Product Notice to pharmacies, distributors, and mail-order companies, urging them to post it where products are stored or sold and to forward it to users. The correction does not require product return, replacement, or removal from use. It affects only the printed and online instructions, including website help guides. Trividia Health has notified the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) and encourages reporting of adverse events through the MedWatch program. The company reiterated that patient safety is its top priority and apologized for any inconvenience. Trividia Health, headquartered in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, is a global provider of diabetes monitoring and wellness solutions, serving major retail pharmacies, distributors, and mail service providers. More details are available at www.trividiahealth.com/E-5productnotice.

    [Original] These Mathematicians Are Trying to Educate A.I.
    A new study titled â€œFirst Proof,â€ led by Fields Medalist Martin Hairer and co-authored by mathematicians Mohammed Abouzaid, Lauren Williams, and Tamara Kolda, aims to objectively assess artificial intelligenceâ€™s capabilities in solving genuine, unsolved research-level math problems. The project responds to growing concerns among students and researchers about AI rendering human mathematicians obsolete, prompted by a recent email from a high school student questioning whether AIâ€™s rapid advancement diminishes mathematicsâ€™ â€œmagic.â€ Hairer, who won the 2014 Fields Medal and 2021 Breakthrough Prize, argues that while AI tools are useful, they have not yet demonstrated the ability to generate truly novel mathematical ideas or concepts. The team designed a benchmark using real, unpublished research questions from their own workâ€”each contributing one problem with a verified solution encrypted and set to be released on February 13. Unlike commercial AI evaluations that rely on â€œcontrivedâ€ or overly narrow problems, often paid for at $5,000 per question, this effort is independent and aims to reflect authentic mathematical research. Abouzaid, a New Horizons Prize winner, declined a prior invitation to such a benchmark, citing the need for broader, public scrutiny. Preliminary tests on OpenAIâ€™s ChatGPT-5.2 Pro and Googleâ€™s Gemini 3.0 Deep Think revealed significant limitations. Systems struggled with complex reasoning, often producing hand-wavy answersâ€”over-explaining simple parts while skipping crucial logic. One model entered an infinite loop, revising its answer repeatedly. Others answered related but different questions. Kolda noted confusion and inconsistency, though she revised the problem statement to improve clarity. Hairer observed that AI excels at assembling known arguments but fails at rigorous, original reasoning, often â€œprayingâ€ with â€œand thereforeâ€ without justification. The paper, published on Euler Day (February 7), draws a parallel to the â€œfirst proofâ€ in bakingâ€”fermenting ideas before shaping them. The team invites the broader mathematical community to engage, with a second, more structured round planned later. While AI is a helpful tool, the authors stress it is not yet a true collaborator. As Williams noted, AI lacks the creative insight and debate-driven dialogue of human colleagues. Kolda warns that overhyped claims could deter students and funders. The goal remains clear: to measure AIâ€™s true limits in advancing mathematical discovery, not to replace the human mind.

    [Original] AutoFlight unveils worldâ€™s largest flying car as China races to lead low-altitude economy
    CATL-backed AutoFlight debuts Matrix, targeting global expansion, as Beijing moves to set standards for domestic eVTOL makers and operators Chinese aviation start-up AutoFlight, backed by electric vehicle (EV) battery giant Contemporary Amperex Technology (CATL), is emblematic of mainland Chinaâ€™s ambitions in the flying car market, part of the countryâ€™s broader push to dominate the low-altitude economy.The Shanghai-based company on Thursday unveiled Matrix, a five-tonne (11,000lbs) class electric vertical take-off and landing (eVTOL) aircraft, which it described as the largest of its kind in the world after completing a flight demonstration at a testing facility in Kunshan, a city neighbouring Shanghai. The aircraft, with a 20-metre (65-foot) wingspan and dimensions of 17.1 metres long by 3.3 metres high, comes in two variants for passenger transport and heavy-duty logistics. It can carry 10 passengers, a leap in scale for an industry that has largely focused on smaller airframes weighing between 1.5 tonnes and 3 tonnes with capacities of four to six passengers. AutoFlight joins peers including Ehang, Xpengâ€™s flying car unit Aridge and Geelyâ€™s Aerofugia as Chinaâ€™s major players in commercial eVTOL applications. The country is moving quickly to set standards for domestic makers and operators, aiming to regulate the skies as the low-altitude economy takes shape. Earlier last week, 10 government departments, including the market regulator and transport ministry, jointly released guidelines to establish basic standards by 2027 and more than 300 standards by 2030. These will cover five core areas: aircraft, infrastructure, air traffic management, safety supervision and application scenarios. Founded in 2017, AutoFlight was currently focused on cargo transport, but saw strong potential in passenger flights, said Xie Jia, senior vice-president of AutoFlight, in an interview.

    [Original] æ˜å† æ–°æï¼šç»ˆæ­¢å¤ªé˜³èƒ½èƒŒæ¿åŠåŠŸèƒ½æ€§è†œç”Ÿäº§åŸºåœ°é¡¹ç›®æŠ•èµ„åè®®
    On February 8, Mingguan New Materials announced that the company has decided to terminate the investment cooperation agreement for the solar backsheet and functional film production base project signed with the Feidong County People's Government. The project was expected to involve a total investment of 5 billion yuan. Currently, the company is actively cooperating with the Feidong County government to complete subsequent procedures such as the completion acceptance of customized properties. Since the fourth quarter of 2023, signs of overcapacity have emerged in the photovoltaic industry, leading to intensified price competition across the industrial chain. The industry is undergoing a period of structural adjustment, resulting in widespread losses across the sector in 2024 and 2025. Based on a thorough analysis and cautious assessment of market changes, the company's management considered that the increasing industry overcapacity has gradually reduced the profitability of photovoltaic encapsulation materials. Moreover, with intensified competition expected in 2025 and no clear signs of improvement in the cyclical adjustment, continuing to advance the Mingguan Hefei project would inevitably raise the company's overall operating costs. (Jiemian News)

    [Original] MAGAâ€™s Split Over Israel Extends to a Ship Attacked 58 Years Ago
    On June 8, 1967, Israeli forces attacked the U.S.S. Liberty, an American intelligence vessel off the Sinai Peninsula, killing 34 crew members and injuring 171. The incident remains a flashpoint in American political discourse, particularly within the MAGA movement, where it has become a divisive litmus test. The official U.S. Navy Court of Inquiry and the Israeli government maintain the attack was a tragic case of mistaken identity during the Six-Day War, a view supported by conservative figures including Senator Ted Cruz, Ben Shapiro, and National Review editor Rich Lowry. However, othersâ€”including Tucker Carlson, Candace Owens, and Representative Paul Gosarâ€”insist Israel intentionally targeted the ship, citing clear weather, the Libertyâ€™s visible U.S. flag, and distinctive hull markings. They allege a cover-up, pointing to statements by then-Secretary of State Dean Rusk calling the attack â€œoutrageousâ€ and not an accident. The debate has surged in recent years, especially amid the Israel-Hamas conflict. In 2022, fewer than 250 daily mentions of the Liberty appeared on X; by 2023, that number had increased tenfold. At Turning Point USAâ€™s 2024 AmericaFest, Liberty-related posts reached 81,000. Owensâ€™ December 2024 podcast with survivor Phil Tourney, who claimed a â€œfalse flagâ€ operation was orchestrated by the U.S. and Israel to provoke American involvement in the war, drew 6.3 million YouTube views. Tourney, 79, president of the Liberty Veterans Association, has since promoted antisemitic conspiracy theories, including blaming Jews for the assassinations of JFK and RFK, the 9/11 attacks, and claims that American politicians are controlled by â€œZionistsâ€â€”though he denies being antisemitic. Younger conservatives are increasingly questioning U.S.-Israel relations.     [Original] The New Fabio Is Claude
    Coral Hart, a veteran romance novelist published by Harlequin and Mills & Boon, launched an eight-month experiment using artificial intelligence to write romance novels under 21 pen names. She produced over 200 books in diverse subgenresâ€”ranging from dark mafia romances to sweet teen storiesâ€”self-published on Amazon, selling approximately 50,000 copies and earning six figures. Using AI, she generated full novels in under an hour, including a rancher-and-city-girl story created in 45 minutes via a prompt-driven system. While AI excelled at speed and volume, Hart found it lacking in emotional nuance, particularly in sex scenes. Programs like Grok and NovelAI produced explicit content but with mechanical, rushed depictions; Claude delivered elegant prose but struggled with banter and often defaulted to clichÃ©d imagery like â€œtangled sheets.â€ Hart developed workaroundsâ€”specific prompts, kink lists, and narrative justificationsâ€”to coax more authentic results, especially from Claude. Despite her advocacy, Hart conceals her AI use under her real name and early pen name, Coral Hart, due to stigma. She plans to launch three new pen names that will openly use AI.     [Original] Fake Post About Racist Video Looked to Be Trumpâ€™s on Truth Social
    A fake post that was designed to look as if it were from President Trumpâ€™s social media feed spread widely online over the weekend, adding confusion to the ongoing debate over Mr. Trumpâ€™s social media activity this week. Posts on X circulating the forgery reached at least 3.7 million views by Saturday. The fake post appeared to describe Mr. Trumpâ€™s rationale for deleting a racist video that he shared earlier this week, which depicted former President Barack Obama and the former first lady, Michelle Obama, as apes. In the fake post that went up on Friday night, Mr. Trump appeared to claim that the video was offensive to animals. Though many users seemed to understand it was fake, some believed it was real, including some right-wing users who praised the president for not apologizing. The user who first published the fake post on X did not immediately respond to a request for comment. Its spread appeared to be aided in part by the confusion surrounding how Mr. Trump came to post the original racist video and why it was deleted. Karoline Leavitt, the White House press secretary, first brushed off the criticism, saying that it was a joke from a longer video depicting several Democrats as jungle animals. Mr. Trump later pushed back on that idea while talking to reporters on Air Force One. He said that he did not err in posting the video but that he had not seen the racist clip â€” which is spliced into another video about voter fraud conspiracy theories â€” before sending it to aides to post on his behalf. â€œI gave it to the people, generally theyâ€™d look at the whole thing but I guess somebody didnâ€™t,â€ he told reporters. The image is part of a surge of fake content that has been circulating online in recent months. A group of right-wing influencers and meme-makers have created scores of artificial-intelligence-generated jokes, videos and satirical political content that is sometimes racist and sexist, racking up millions of views. Mr. Trump has elevated their work before. In October, Mr. Trump posted an A.I.-generated video of himself piloting a fighter jet and dropping excrement on protesters. The user who created the fighter jet video also created the racist video of the Obamas. Stuart A.     [Original] Prediction Markets and Casinos Go to War Over Sports Betting
    In just eight years, sports gambling in the U.S. has grown from an illegal enterprise to a $220 billion annual industry, with $1.8 billion expected to be wagered on Super Bowl LX. Traditional sportsbooks like DraftKings, FanDuel, and BetMGM now face competition from prediction markets such as Kalshi and Polymarket, which by one estimate divert $8 billion annually from sportsbooks. These platforms argue they are not subject to state gambling laws because they operate under federal regulation by the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC), not state gaming commissions. The 2018 Supreme Court decision that struck down the federal ban on sports betting left regulation to individual states, with 39 states and Washington, D.C. now allowing sports betting. However, prediction markets allow users in non-legal states to bet, prompting legal pushback. At least 20 federal lawsuits have been filed, including a class-action suit against Polymarket in New York, and state officials like New York Attorney General Letitia James have warned consumers about unregulated gambling. The American Gaming Association (A.G.A.) and Indian Gaming Association have urged Congress to regulate prediction markets, claiming theyâ€™ve cost states over $400 million in tax revenue. In response, a coalition of companies including Kalshi, Robinhood, and Coinbase formed the Coalition for Prediction Markets, with Kalshi hiring Donald Trump Jr. as a strategic adviser. The CFTC has backed prediction markets, with Chairman Michael S. Selig affirming its jurisdiction and withdrawing a Biden-era rule that would have banned political and sports-related contracts. However, courts have issued early rulings against them: a Nevada judge blocked Kalshi from offering sports contracts, and Massachusetts and Ohio have secured injunctions. Kalshiâ€™s data shows $12.5 billion in sports-related volumeâ€”90% of its transaction feesâ€”making a ban potentially catastrophic. Analysts like Chad Beynon of Macquarie Group argue the threat is overstated, noting prediction markets lack popular features like parlays and in-play betting, and most users are from states without legal sports betting. Meanwhile, traditional sportsbooks are adapting: FanDuel, DraftKings, and Fanatics have launched their own prediction markets, citing a â€œlack of alignmentâ€ with the A.G.A. These companies can fall back on their core models if regulation tightens. The long-term outcome hinges on political shifts, with analysts warning that a Democratic administration could target prediction markets, making current investments risky.

    [Original] Binance Gives Trump Familyâ€™s Crypto Firm a Leg Up
    World Liberty Financial, the Trump familyâ€™s cryptocurrency venture, reached a $5 billion circulation milestone for its stablecoin, USD1, marking a major achievement in the digital asset space. The companyâ€™s success is largely attributed to a strategic alliance with Binance, the worldâ€™s largest crypto exchange, founded by Changpeng Zhao. Over 85% of USD1 coins are held on Binance, despite the platformâ€™s restricted access in the United States. Binance has offered fee-free trading and interest-bearing promotions on USD1, including a $40 million reward pool announced in January, which spurred nearly $2 billion in global trading within a week. The relationship has drawn scrutiny from ethics experts and lawmakers, who cite a conflict of interest as President Trump, now both a crypto entrepreneur and the nationâ€™s top policymaker, pardoned Zhao in October after he served four months in prison for money-laundering violations. Zhao remains Binanceâ€™s majority shareholder, and the pardon has raised concerns about potential quid pro quo arrangements, especially as Binance has expanded its ties with World Liberty. The exchange has facilitated major deals, including a $2 billion investment by MGX, a UAE-backed firm, conducted entirely in USD1â€”the largest stablecoin transaction to date. World Liberty, co-led by Trumpâ€™s sons and Steve Witkoffâ€™s family, has invested deposits in government money-market funds, generating an estimated $200 million in annual revenue from $5 billion in assets. The companyâ€™s spokesman stated that promotional incentives were funded by World Liberty and are standard practice, while Binance emphasized that it offers similar programs for various tokens and complies with global regulations. A White House spokesperson confirmed Trumpâ€™s assets are held in a trust managed by his children, denying conflicts of interest. The GENIUS Act, signed by Trump in 2023, prohibits stablecoin issuers from offering interest, but allows exchanges to do soâ€”creating a regulatory loophole. Binanceâ€™s interest programs on USD1 exploit this gap, raising concerns among banking lobbyists who fear competition with traditional savings accounts. Critics argue such arrangements could undermine financial stability and fall into the very loopholes Congress aims to close. Despite the controversy, Binance and World Liberty continue to deepen their partnership, with Binanceâ€™s co-CEO Yi He, who has children with Zhao, overseeing operations since December. The White House maintains that all actions are lawful and transparent.

    [Original] Washington Post publisher Will Lewis announces departure, following mass layoffs
    Washington Post publisher and CEO Will Lewis is leaving the newspaper, the company announced on Saturday after carrying out widespread layoffs this week. "During my tenure, difficult decisions have been taken in order to ensure the sustainable future of The Post so it can for many years ahead publish high-quality nonpartisan news to millions of customers each day," Lewis wrote in a message to staff that was shared online by the newspaper's White House bureau chief, Matt Viser. Lewis, a former Dow Jones chief executive and publisher of the Wall Street Journal, was appointed to the role at the Washington Post in 2023 as the newspaper was suffering steep financial losses. He took over from Fred Ryan, who had served as publisher and CEO for nearly a decade. Jeff D'Onofrio, chief financial officer of the newspaper owned by Jeff Bezos, will serve as acting publisher and CEO, the Post said. He joined the newspaper last June after serving in various roles at Google and Yahoo, among other companies. "Customer data will drive our decisions, sharpening our edge in delivering what is most valuable to our audiences," D'Onofrio wrote on Saturday in an email to Post staffers. Unions representing Post employees said Lewis' departure was necessary. "Will Lewis's exit is long overdue," The Washington Post Guild said in a statement. "His legacy will be the attempted destruction of a great American journalism institution. But it's not too late to save the Post. Jeff Bezos must immediately rescind these layoffs or sell the paper to someone willing to invest in its future." Bezos, who bought the newspaper in 2013, characterized the leadership change as an "extraordinary opportunity" for the newspaper. "The Post has an essential journalistic mission and an extraordinary opportunity," Bezos said, according to the Post. "Each and every day our readers give us a roadmap to success." The departure of Lewis came days after the Post cut about one-third of its employees in a move that affected all departments at the newspaper. He was criticized for his absence during the layoffs on Wednesday, which the newspaper's former executive editor, Marty Baron, described as "among the darkest days" in the newspaper's history. During his time at the Post, Lewis oversaw waves of staff reductions and had to deal with the loss of hundreds of thousands of subscribers after the newspaper stopped endorsing U.S. presidential candidates and shifted its opinion section's emphasis to a libertarian bent. Lewis' Post tenure was rocky even before the subscriber losses. After a 2024 disagreement with then-executive editor Sally Buzbee led to her departure, Lewis faced a newsroom outcry over his attempt to hire British journalist and former colleague Robert Winnett, who was linked to a phone-hacking controversy that also involved Lewis. Meanwhile, Lewis' most ballyhooed initiative, a so-called third newsroom, never came to fruition. Former Wall Street Journal editor Matt Murray eventually was named the permanent replacement for Buzbee, who is now Reuters' news editor for the United States and Canada.

    [Original] Polls close in Thai election pitting reformists against conservatives
    Thailandâ€™s early general election, called after three prime ministers in three years and collapsing coalitions, has concluded with vote counting underway, results expected by 22:00 local time (15:00 GMT). The contest pitted reformist forces, represented by the Peopleâ€™s Party led by Nattaphong Ruengpanyawut, against conservative incumbent Prime Minister Anutin Charnavirakul and his Bhumjaithai party, which has evolved from a provincial outfit into the standard-bearer for Thai conservatism. Early results, with 18% of votes counted, show Bhumjaithai leading with a projected 178 constituency seats, compared to the Peopleâ€™s Partyâ€™s 70. Pheu Thai, the Shinawatra familyâ€™s party, is a third major contender, though it faces declining support after its last coalition was criticized for mishandling the 2023 border conflict with Cambodia and following the imprisonment of patriarch Thaksin Shinawatra. Pheu Thai has promised to create nine new millionaires daily through a national prize draw and offered voter subsidies. Despite economic stagnation and rising costs fueling voter concernâ€”civil servant Phananya Bunthong cited Thailand falling behind Vietnamâ€”Anutin has capitalized on patriotic sentiment, emphasizing defense of the monarchy, military, and traditional institutions. The Peopleâ€™s Party advocates sweeping reforms, including curbing business and military power, streamlining bureaucracy, and modernizing education. However, past reformist parties have been dissolved by the constitutional court, and their leaders banned from politics. The Peopleâ€™s Partyâ€™s 2023 victory of 151 seats may now be a threshold: if it exceeds that number, blocking its government formation may become politically difficult, though further intervention by courts or unelected bodies is expected. If Bhumjaithai matches or surpasses the reformistsâ€™ seat count, with conservative establishment backing, Anutin is likely to remain PM. A separate referendum on amending the 2017 constitutionâ€”drafted under military ruleâ€”also took place. Critics argue it grants excessive power to unelected bodies like the senate, effectively â€œhandcuffingâ€ democracy. â€œI want change. I donâ€™t want things to be the same,â€ said 28-year-old voter Kittitat Daengkongkho, reflecting a broader voter sentiment. The election thus presented a clear choice: radical transformation or continuity with Thailandâ€™s entrenched power structures.

    [Original] Man named in South Africa's police corruption probe found dead
    ShareSaveDamian ZaneShareSaveGetty ImagesA South African man named in a major police corruption probe has died after reportedly shooting himself at a petrol station. Police are now investigating the death of Wiandre Pretorius, 41, who last week said he had survived an assassination attempt. Pretorius's name had been mentioned at the ongoing corruption inquiry, known as the Madlanga Commission. This was in connection with the 2022 murder of a witness, Emmanuel Mbense, allegedly at the hands of police officers. Four of the 12 people named as persons of interest in that killing are now dead themselves, a police spokesperson said. At 22:00 local time (20:00 GMT) on Saturday the police received reports that a man had taken his own life at a petrol station in Brakpan, east of Johannesburg. At the scene, officers found Pretorius's body with a firearm next to it, spokesperson Brig Athlenda Mathe said. The police are now looking at CCTV footage to confirm what happened. There had been reports that Pretorius had been involved in a row with his fiancÃ©e at the petrol station before taking his own life. The murder four years ago of Mbense is one of several issues that has come up at the Madlanga Commission, which was set up by President Cyril Ramaphosa after a senior police officer alleged that organised crime groups had infiltrated the government. At a hearing last year, a man, only identified at the time as Witness D, said that in 2022 he had been ordered to get rid of the body of someone accused of robbery who had allegedly been tortured and killed by police officers. Witness D also alleged that Pretorius, who was not a policeman but had previously served as a police reservist, was involved. The witness, later named as Marius van der Merwe, was shot death three weeks after testifying. Police spokesperson Mathe said on Sunday that Pretorius had been questioned and his firearms confiscated in connection with Van der Merwe's killing. Mathe added that the death of Pretorius on Saturday night leaves only eight of the original 12 persons of interest in the killing of Mbense still alive. Three were killed "execution style" â€“ one in 2023 and two last year. "The question is: are we dealing with a syndicate that is eliminating each other in relation to the Emmanel Mbense murder? That is what our detectives are probing," Mathe told reporters. Last week, police began investigating whether Pretorius himself had been the target of an assassination attempt after he said that his vehicle had been shot at. In connection with the murder of Mbense, Mathe said that "arrests are imminent" following an investigation by the independent police watchdog body.     [Original] 3 Doors Down lead singer Brad Arnold dies at 47
    ShareSaveKayla EpsteinShareSaveGetty ImagesThe lead singer and songwriter of 3 Doors Down, Brad Arnold, has died after a battle with cancer aged 47, the rock band announced on X. "He will be deeply missed and forever remembered," the band said in a statement on Saturday. The band is best known for 2000s rock hits like Kryptonite, Here Without You, When I'm Gone, and Loser. Arnold had announced in May 2025 that he was ill and had received a diagnosis of stage four clear cell renal carcinoma - a type of kidney cancer - which had metastasised into his lung. "I have no fear, I really sincerely am not scared of it at all," the frontman said, adding that he was disappointed that the band would have to cancel an upcoming tour. "I'd love for you to lift me up in prayer every chance you get," he said. In its statement, 3 Doors Down said that, as a founding member, vocalist, and original drummer, "Brad helped redefine mainstream rock music, blending post-grunge accessibility with emotionally direct song writing and lyrical themes that resonated with everyday listeners". The original band was formed in Mississippi in the mid-1990s. Another founding member of the original trio, Matt Roberts, died in 2016 at the age of 38. Arnold wrote Kryptonite, the band's 2000 breakout hit, "in his math class when he was just 15 years old", the statement continued. Those closest to Arnold will "remember not only his talent, but his warmth, humility, faith, and deep love for his family and friends", it said. The band was regularly heard on rock and pop radio throughout the 2000s and 2010s. They have won three Billboard Music Awards. Their debut album The Better Life was the 11th biggest-selling album of the year in their home country. Arnold had spoken openly about hit battle with alcoholism and his recovery, having been sober since 2016. "I used to think it was a way to calm myself prior to a show or to chase loneliness," he told Charleston.com in 2023. The band performed for the inauguration of US President George W Bush as well as the first inauguration of President Donald Trump, which received some criticism from fans. Their manager, Angus Vail, defended the decision to perform for the 2017 Trump presidential celebration, telling Vice: "They are good Mississippi and Alabama boys - they come from conservative families." In 2004, 3 Doors Down established a charity, the Better Life Foundation, to create "positive change in the lives of children in need of food, shelter and medical assistance". The band hosts a yearly concert to raise funds for the organisation. "All the money that goes into that [charity] comes from fans, and people, that they give to us," Arnold told Antihero magazine in 2021. "But being able to see what that's done over the years has definitely enriched my life."

    [Original] Australia's opposition coalition reunites after row over hate-speech laws
    ShareSaveChris GrahamShareSaveReutersSussan Ley said it was time to look to the future. Australia's Liberal-National Coalition, the country's main opposition, reunited on Sunday, more than two weeks after the centre-right partners split in a row over hate speech laws. "The Coalition is back together and looking to the future, not to the past," Liberal Party leader Sussan Ley said, appearing alongside National Party leader David Littleproud in Canberra. The Coalition split on 22 January after the Nationals, citing free speech concerns, refused to back reforms moved by the government after two gunmen targeted a Jewish festival at Bondi Beach in December, killing 15 people. "It's been disappointing, we've got to where we are but it was over a substantive issue," Littleproud said. The Coalition suffered a heavy election loss last year and the split last month was the second in less than 12 months. Last year's separation in May - largely over climate and energy policy - was resolved within a week. This time the divisions were sown by hate speech reforms introduced by the centre-left Labor government after the Bondi Beach attack. While the Liberals sided with the government, their National colleagues abstained from the vote in the lower house and voted against the measure in the senate, saying the measures had been rushed and posed a threat to free speech. The legislation includes provisions that will ban groups deemed to spread hate and introduce tougher penalties for preachers who advocate violence. Ley said the coalition had a responsibility to find a way back to government. "I acknowledge this has been a difficult time. It has been a difficult time for millions of our Coalition supporters, and many other Australians who rely on our two great parties to provide scrutiny and leadership," she said. The Liberal Party leader said both parties had struck an agreement that neither party could overturn decisions taken by the Coalition's joint "shadow cabinet". Dating back to the 1940s, the Coalition had not split since 1987 before the brief separation last year. The National Party mainly represents regional communities and often leans more conservative than the Liberals. The Coalition is facing pressure from populist Senator Pauline Hanson's anti-immigration One Nation party, which has surged in polling, while the Liberal Party lost a swath of seats at last year's federal election.

    As indirect talks begin between the U.S. and Iran over that country's nuclear program, Ryan Fayhee, lawyer for journalist Abdolreza Valizadeh, talks about his concern for his client, who is being held in Evin prison in Tehran.

    [Original] England beat Nepal by 4 runs; avoid shock at T20 World Cup
    Listen to this article | 2 minsinfoNepal's captain Rohit Paudel and his team were left disappointed at the end of the cricket match as they lost to England by four runs at the Wankhede Stadium in Mumbai, India [Indranil Mukherjee/AFP]By Hafsa Adil and News AgenciesPublished On 8 Feb 20268 Feb 2026Click here to share on social mediashare2Share Nepal were left heartbroken after they came agonisingly close to pulling off a massive T20 World Cup upset against England but fell short by four runs as the two-time champions won the Group C match in Mumbai. Lokesh Bamâ€™s heroics with the bat â€“ 39 runs off 20 balls â€“ were not enough to see Nepal over the line at the Wankhede Stadium, which was packed with Nepalese fans on Sunday. Nepal finished on 180-6, handing England a nervy win to kick off their campaign in the controversy-hit cricket tournament. When Englandâ€™s captain Harry Brook (53) and teammate Jacob Bethell (55) hit fifties to power England to 184-7, they seemingly did enough to take the match out of Nepalâ€™s reach. But Rohit Paudel produced a captainâ€™s innings of his own as he, alongside star all-rounder Dipendra Singh Airee, put Nepal on course for a shock win. The pairâ€™s departure slowed down Nepalâ€™s progress, but Lokesh resumed the big hitting against some wayward bowling by Englandâ€™s seamers. The Rhinosâ€™ fans, hundreds of whom had travelled from across the border, were left disheartened.     [Original] TikTok deal good for Chinese owners but terrible for users in the United States
    The social media platform, now majority owned by Americans, will herald a new era of state control and corporate manipulation of US citizens If American users of TikTok think its transition to majority US ownership would make it more secure and freer, they are sorely mistaken. Rather, they should expect the opposite. Some 170 million TikTokkers received a pop-up message telling them that if they wanted to continue with the service, they had to agree to new terms of service and privacy policy under new US majority ownership. Users almost immediately sensed a difference in the online environment. There were news reports that the social media platform may be censoring political speech and sensitive content. According to CNBC, â€œAgainst the backdrop of a tense political environment in the US, a growing number of viral complaints about TikTok have accused the platform of censoring certain political positions and even the word â€˜Epsteinâ€™ within direct messaging. CNBC confirmed that messages containing the word â€˜Epsteinâ€™ triggered an error message, but was unable to independently verify broader claims of political censorship.â€ CNN and BBC reported that TikTok users could not upload videos about brutality committed by ICE agents, a federal paramilitary force carrying out anti-immigrant operations, especially in Minnesota. TikTok America blamed technical glitches. Yeah, sure, whatever. Perhaps no one should be surprised. The forced sale of the hugely popular platform was never about censorship, surveillance or disinformation potentially spread under Chinese ownership. Itâ€™s always been about the ability of the political and media establishment in the US to do all that out of reach of the Chinese.

    Emergency crews remain at the site in Shanxi province as smoke continues to billow from the wreckage Eight people have been confirmed dead in a blast at a biotechnology factory in central China early on Saturday. The explosion ripped through a workshop in Shanyin county, Shanxi province, operated by Jiapeng Biotechnology, a company involved in bio-feed, coal and related products, building materials, and paint manufacturing. The county government said the rescue operation had concluded and the companyâ€™s legal representative had been taken into police custody. Officials from Shuozhou, the city overseeing the county, were investigating the cause of the incident, municipal authorities said. Emergency crews were still at the site on Sunday, where dark yellow smoke continued to rise from the wreckage, state news agency Xinhua reported.

    [Original] AutoFlight unveils worldâ€™s largest flying car as China races to lead low-altitude economy
    CATL-backed AutoFlight debuts Matrix, targeting global expansion, as Beijing moves to set standards for domestic eVTOL makers and operators Chinese aviation start-up AutoFlight, backed by electric vehicle (EV) battery giant Contemporary Amperex Technology (CATL), is emblematic of mainland Chinaâ€™s ambitions in the flying car market, part of the countryâ€™s broader push to dominate the low-altitude economy.The Shanghai-based company on Thursday unveiled Matrix, a five-tonne (11,000lbs) class electric vertical take-off and landing (eVTOL) aircraft, which it described as the largest of its kind in the world after completing a flight demonstration at a testing facility in Kunshan, a city neighbouring Shanghai. The aircraft, with a 20-metre (65-foot) wingspan and dimensions of 17.1 metres long by 3.3 metres high, comes in two variants for passenger transport and heavy-duty logistics. It can carry 10 passengers, a leap in scale for an industry that has largely focused on smaller airframes weighing between 1.5 tonnes and 3 tonnes with capacities of four to six passengers. AutoFlight joins peers including Ehang, Xpengâ€™s flying car unit Aridge and Geelyâ€™s Aerofugia as Chinaâ€™s major players in commercial eVTOL applications. The country is moving quickly to set standards for domestic makers and operators, aiming to regulate the skies as the low-altitude economy takes shape. Earlier last week, 10 government departments, including the market regulator and transport ministry, jointly released guidelines to establish basic standards by 2027 and more than 300 standards by 2030. These will cover five core areas: aircraft, infrastructure, air traffic management, safety supervision and application scenarios. Founded in 2017, AutoFlight was currently focused on cargo transport, but saw strong potential in passenger flights, said Xie Jia, senior vice-president of AutoFlight, in an interview.

    [Original] China executed a series of Myanmese crime bosses. What does it say about its regional influence?
    The condemned headed family syndicates that trapped Chinese abroad in massive scam centres In less than a week, China conducted a series of executions on a scale rarely seen in recent decades.In all, 16 core members of mafia-like crime syndicates were put to death for a range of crimes, from murder to fraud and human trafficking. Yet, China was able to convince authorities in Myanmar to hand over suspects. Observers said Southeast Asian countries might have little choice but to acquiesce, with China showing â€œmerciless resolveâ€ to protect the interests of its citizens abroad.
